Certification of Compliance with Driver License Requirements

Motor Carrier Instructions: The requirements in Part 383 apply to every driver who operates in intrastate, interstate, or foreign commerce and operates a vehicle weighing or rated at 26,001 pounds or more, can. transport more than 15 people, or transports hazardous materials that require placarding.

The requirements in Part 391 apply to every driver who operates in interstate commerce and operates a vehicle weighing or rated at 10,001 pounds or more, can transport more than 15 people (or more than 8 people when there is direct compensation), or transports hazardous materials that require placarding.

Driver Requirements: Parts 383 and 391 of the Federal Motor Carrier Safety Regulations contain certain driver licensing requirements that you as a driver must comply with, including the following:

1. Possess only one license: You, as a commercial vehicle driver, may not possess more than one motor vehicle operator’s license.

2. Notification of License suspension, revocation or cancellation: Sections 391.15 (b)(2) and 383.33 of the Federal Motor Carrier Safety Regulations require that you notify your employer the NEXT BUSINESS DAY of any revocation, suspension, cancellation or disqualification of your driver’s license or driving privilege. In addition, Section 383.31 requires that any time you are convicted of violating a state or local traffic law (other than parking), you must report it within 30 days to your employing motor carrier. The notification must be made in writing.

3. CDL Domicile Requirement: Section 383.23 (a)(2) requires that your commercial driver’s license be issued by your legal state of domicile, where you have your true, fixed, and permanent home and principal residence and to which you have the intention of returning whenever you are absent. If you establish a new domicile in another state, you must apply to transfer your CDL within 30 days.

Driver Statement: the following license is the only one I possess:

Driver’s License No. 4 A Y YS. r4 Y c State _/ Et Expiration Date UfZ?

Drivers Certification: I certify that I have read and understand the above requirements.

Driver’s Name _ (Printed):

Driver’s Signature:

OHIO DEPARTMENT OF PUBLIC SAFETY BUREAU OF MOTOR VEHICLES

CDL SELF-CERTIFICATION AUTHORIZATION

Effective January 30, 2012, new federal regulations require ALL Commercial Driver License (CDL) holders to self-certify their type of commercial driving. All CDL holders must submit a self-certification in order to be issued and maintain their CDL.

OHIO DRIVER LICENSE NUMBER

VA CES.

Please mark only one of the following self-certification categories that apply to you. (see page 2 for category detail)

1 certify my commercial driving is:

Category 1: Non-Excepted Interstate: CDL holders who drive across state lines or transport freight that has or will cross state lines and must meet federal medical requirements subject to 49 CFR part 391. (Must submit medical card to Ohio BMV)

[_] Category 2: Excepted Interstate: CDL holders who drive across state lines but do not need to meet federal medical requirements. Operating exclusively in transportation or operations excepted under 49 CFR 390.3(f), 391.2, 39168 or 398.3

[_] Category 3: Non-Excepted Intrastate: CDL holders who drive exclusively in Ohio and do not drive across state lines, but are required to meet state medical requirements.

[-] Category 4: Excepted Intrastate: CDL holders who do not use the CDL for business purposes and are not

required to meet state medical requirements. Operating exclusively in transportation or operations excepted from all or part of the State driver qualification requirements. (R.C. 4506.03(B)(1-10))

SIGNATURE OF APPLICANT DATE

If you mark category 1, you must also submit a copy of your completed Medical Examiners Certificate.

fall ‘I have included a Medical Examiners Certificate.

The CDL Self-Certification Authorization form and the Medical Examiners Certificate, if applicable, must be submitted to the Ohio Bureau of Motor Vehicles and processed prior to the issuance of the CDL. The Self-Certification Authorization form and the Medical Examiners Certificate can be submitted by mail, fax, e-mail, Regional Reinstatement Office or a Deputy Registrar. The forms must be legible or a delay in processing will occur.

THE BELOW DISCLOSURE AND AUTHORIZATION LANGUAGE IS FOR MANDATORY USE BY ALL ACCOUNT HOLDERS

IMPORTANT DISCLOSURE REGARDING BACKGROUND REPORTS FROM THE PSP Online Service

In connection with your application for employment with Crete Carrier Corporation (“Prospective Employer”), Prospective Employer, its employees, agents or contractors may obtain one or more reports regarding your driving, and safety inspection history from the Federal Motor Carrier Safety Administration (FMCSA).

When the application for employment is submitted in person, if the Prospective Employer uses any information it obtains from FMCSA in a decision to not hire you or to make any other adverse employment decision regarding you, the Prospective Employer will provide you with a copy of the report upon which its decision was based and a written summary of your rights under the Fair Credit Reporting Act before taking any final adverse action. If any final adverse action is taken against you based upon your driving history or safety report, the Prospective Employer will notify you that the action has been taken and that the action was based in part or in whole on this report.

When the application for employment is submitted by mail, telephone, computer, or other similar means, if the Prospective Employer uses any information it obtains from FMCSA in a decision to not hire you or to make any other adverse employment decision regarding you, the Prospective Employer must provide you within three business days of taking adverse action oral, written or electronic notification: that adverse action has been taken based in whole or in part on information obtained from FMCSA; the name, address, and the toll free telephone number of FMCSA; that the FMCSA did not make the decision to take the adverse action and is unable to provide you the specific reasons why the adverse action was taken; and that you may, upon providing proper identification, request a free copy of the report and may dispute with the FMCSA the accuracy or completeness of any information or report. If you request a copy of a driver record from the Prospective Employer who procured the report, then, within 3 business days of receiving your request, together with proper identification, the Prospective Employer must send or provide to you a copy of your report and a summary of your rights under the Fair Credit Reporting Act.

Neither the Prospective Employer nor the FMCSA contractor supplying the crash and safety information has the capability to correct any safety data that appears to be incorrect. You may challenge the accuracy of the data by submitting a request to https://dataqs.fmcesa.dot.gov. If you challenge crash or inspection information reported by a State, FMCSA cannot change or correct this data. Your request will be forwarded by the DataQs system to the appropriate State for adjudication.

Any crash or inspection in which you were involved will display on your PSP report. Since the PSP report does not report, or assign, or imply fault, it will include all Commercial Motor Vehicle (CMV) crashes where you were a driver or co-driver and where those crashes were reported to FMCSA, regardless of fault. Similarly, all inspections, with or without violations, appear on the PSP report. State citations associated with Federal Motor Carrier Safety Regulations (FMCSR) violations that have been adjudicated by a court of law will also appear, and remain, on a PSP report.

The Prospective Employer cannot obtain background reports from FMCSA without your authorization.

AUTHORIZATION

If you agree that the Prospective Employer may obtain such background reports, please read the following and sign below:

I authorize Crete Carrier Corporation (“Prospective Employer”) to access the FMCSA Pre-Employment Screening Program (PSP) system to seek information regarding my commercial driving safety record and information regarding my safety inspection history. I understand that I am authorizing the release of safety performance information including crash data from the previous five (5) years and inspection history from the previous three (3) years. I understand and acknowledge that this release of information may assist the Prospective Employer to make a determination regarding my suitability as an employee.

I further understand that neither the Prospective Employer nor the FMCSA contractor supplying the crash and safety information has the capability to correct any safety data that appears to be incorrect. I understand I may challenge the accuracy of the data by submitting a request to https://dataqs.fmcsa.dot.gov. If I challenge crash or inspection information reported by a State, FMCSA cannot change or correct this data. I understand my request will be forwarded by the DataQs system to the appropriate State for adjudication.

I understand that any crash or inspection in which I was involved will display on my PSP report. Since the PSP report does not

report, or assign, or imply fault, I acknowledge it will include all CMV crashes where I was a driver or co-driver and where those crashes were reported to FMCSA, regardless of fault. Similarly, I understand all inspections, with or without violations, will appear

ELECTRONIC TOLL TRANSPONDER USAGE AGREEMENT

1, Roy Hamilton , acknowledge that I am responsible for the company issued electronic toll transponder assigned to my tractor. I will immediately notify the Licensing and Permits Department in Lincoln, NE (800- 998-9100 ext. 42) if the unit is lost, damaged, destroyed or is malfunctioning.

I understand the transponder is assigned by tractor unit number to the tractor I will be driving and cannot and should not be used in any other vehicle. I will contact the Licensing and Permits Department at the telephone number reflected above to obtain a transponder if I change tractors and the tractor to which I am assigned does not contain a transponder.

I agree to keep toll costs to a minimum by following the suggested routing instructions given to me at the time I am dispatched on a load.

I understand I will be required and do hereby agree to reimburse Crete Carrier Corporation or the Shaffer Trucking Division through a payroll or trip settlement deduction, any toll charges resulting from the unauthorized or improper use of this electronic toll collection device.

Unauthorized or improper use includes, but is not limited to:

e Usage when not under dispatch, unless authorized by dispatch.

e Usage in any other vehicle except the tractor which I own (Owner-Operator) or to which I am assigned (Company Driver).

e Fines or charges, if any, imposed by the toll road regulatory agencies for not following the specific instructions imposed at toll collection sites.

e Failure to notify the Licensing and Permit Department immediately at the phone number referenced above if the unit is lost, damaged, stolen or is malfunctioning.

e Not adhering to specific load assignment suggested routing instructions resulting in unauthorized toll charges.

Consent for Limited Queries of the Federal Motor Carrier Safety Administration (FMCSA) Drug and Alcohol Clearinghouse

I hereby provide consent to Crete Carrier Corporation and its division of Shaffer Trucking (hereinafter collectively referred to as "Crete Carrier Corporation") to conduct a limited query of the FMCSA Commercial Driver's License Drug and Alcohol Clearinghouse to determine whether drug or alcohol violation information about me exists in the Clearinghouse. I understand this consent shall remain on file and shall serve as ongoing consent for Crete Carrier Corporation to conduct multiple limited queries of the Clearinghouse at any time during my employment or contract period without asking me for additional consent.

I understand that if I refuse to provide consent for Crete Carrier Corporation to conduct a limited query of the Clearinghouse, Crete Carrier Corporation is required to prohibit me from performing safety-sensitive functions, including operating a commercial motor vehicle.

I understand that if the limited query conducted by Crete Carrier Corporation indicates that drug or alcohol information exists about me in the Clearinghouse, the FMCSA will not disclose that information to Crete Carrier Corporation unless I give additional specific consent within the Clearinghouse. However, I understand that Crete Carrier Corporation will be required to conduct a full query of the Clearinghouse within 24 hours after a limited query indicates that drug or alcohol information exists and that if I do not grant consent within the Clearinghouse for that full query I will be removed from performing safety-sensitive functions, including operating a commercial motor vehicle.

ONBOARD COMMUNICATIONS EQUIPMENT AGREEMENT (Company Driver)

This constitutes the agreement of the driver whose signature appears below with respect to the use of the Onboard Communications unit (the “Unit’) installed by Crete Carrier Corporation and its operating division Shaffer Trucking (“the Company’) on tractors I operate on the Company’s behalf.

I acknowledge that I have been informed by the Company that operation of the Unit by the driver while the tractor is in motion may bb DANGEROUS and that the Company has therefore ordered and instructed me NOT TO USE OR PERMIT THE UNIT TO BE USED WHILE THE TRACTOR IS IN MOTION.

As a single driver, I agree that I|WILL NOT OPERATE OR PERMIT THE OPERATION OF THE UNIT WHILE THE VEHICLE IS IN MOTION. I have been advised, and I acknowledge and agree, that a violation of this commitment may result in disciplinary action being taken against me and could result in my being held personally liable for any personal injury or property damage which I cause.

As a team driver, I agree that WHILE DRIVING, OR WHILE THE VEHICLE IS IN MOTION, I WILL NOT OPERATE THE UNIT. THE UNIT MAY BE OPERATED WHILE THE VEHICLE IS IN MOTION, BUT ONLY BY THE NON-DRIVING TEAM DRIVER. I have been advised, and I acknowledge and agree, that a violation of this commitment may result in disciplinary action being taken against me and could result in my being held personally liable for any personal injury or property damage I cause.

I agree that I will not tamper with or abuse the Unit or allow anyone else to do so and that I will not do anything to the Unit, which will interfere with its performance or operation.

I agree that I will be responsible for any loss or damage to the Unit caused by my negligence or willful misconduct and I authorize the Company to deduct from my wages the amount of any expense resulting from my failure to return the Unit in an undamaged condition.

This document contains a statement of important legal consequences including the loss of liability insurance coverage. READ IT CAREFULLY BEFORE SIGNING. DO NOT SIGN THIS DOCUMENT IF YOU DO NOT UNDERSTAND IT.

I hereby acknowledge that I have been informed that the policy of Crete Carrier Corporation and its operating division of Shaffer Trucking (“the Company’) and the provisions of Section 392.60 of the Federal Motor Carrier Safety Regulations prohibit the transportation of unauthorized passengers at any time or under any circumstances in commercial motor vehicles.

LOAD DISPATCH POLICY COMPANY DRIVER

All Company drivers providing over the road or dedicated driving services for the Company and

transporting freight in a Customer Dedicated Operation will be treated equally with respect to the dispatch of available freight. Our objectives are to safely provide quality service to our customers, minimize empty miles, and maximize the utilization of all available equipment.

As a Company driver, available loads will be planned for you and you will receive from the Operations Department dispatcher one planned load. If you are available for dispatch and have hours of service remaining to pick up and/or transport the load, you are required to accept the planned load offered. Planned loads will be determined by the dispatcher based on the following:

1. Driver’s ability to safely pick up and/or deliver the load on time within the Hours of Service requirements of the Department of Transportation.

2. Best service to our customer.

3. The optimum match of all available freight and equipment to maximize productivity and minimize deadhead miles.

With proper notice, every effort will be made to incorporate a driver’s personal needs with respect to getting to a specific location.

Company drivers who meet the criteria for being able to accept, legally pick up, and safely transport freight as offered, may be removed from service or suspended from active driving duties for refusing a dispatch or other violations of Company policies.

If at any time your electronic communications unit is malfunctioning, you will need to check-call at least once every twelve (12) hours by telephone to inform the Operations Department (Dispatch) of your location, availability for dispatch and any other information you may have which may affect the timely pickup, transit, or delivery of your load. This information is essential to properly plan the solicitation and acceptance of freight from our customers. Without exception, you are required to send an electronic message to the Operations Department when you have T-called a load or delivered your load and your trailer is empty, even if you are going out of service for any period of time.

GENERAL RULES OF CONDUCT AND AUTHORIZATION

I am currently a driver, or have completed preliminary processing in connection with my application for employment as a driver, for Crete Carrier Corporation or its operating division Shaffer Trucking (the “Company’). I understand my employment commenced, employment as a qualified driver commenced, or will commence, at Company Headquarters upon the approval of my application and my completion of Driver Orientation.

I understand the following are general rules of conduct for Company drivers. These general rules are not all inclusive and I acknowledge there are other Company policies and procedures I must follow. As a Company driver, I will abide by the following general rules of conduct and all other Company policies and procedures. I understand that if I do not comply with these rules and other Company policies and procedures, I may be subject to disciplinary action and/or termination of employment.

1.

oo3en

Driver Duties. As a driver, I will:

send or make daily hours of service and other required mobilecom transmissions, check calls and messages to the Operations Department

communicate at least weekly with my assigned Fleet Manager

consent to receive text messages sent by an automatic telephone dialing system, which may transmit important information or requests for feedback on your experience as an employee. You may opt out at any time by texting STOP to unsubscribe, but you may thereafter not be informed of important information sent in this way.

maintain a clean truck both inside and out

perform loading and unloading of freight if requested

insure that all equipment and paperwork in my possession complies with Department of Transportation regulations and Company policies and procedures

insure my tractor-trailer unit is of legal weight for travel at all times and that my tandems are properly and legally set for states through which the load will travel from the point of origin to destination

submit all required trip and regulatory paper work immediately upon completion of delivery of a load

include the odometer reading from my Company truck on all fuel tickets and repair receipts submitted to the Company when necessary, clean the inside of Company trailers prior to loading and after unloading and, if applicable, refuel refrigeration units before dropping a refrigerated trailer for reloading

promptly report to Acklie Maintenance Systems any and all tractor or trailer damage or any past due required maintenance and assist in getting the equipment serviced when needed

as soon as practically possible report any accidents or any OS&D or claims issue

return all Company equipment to a designated Company location immediately upon the termination of my employment, regardless of the cause for the termination

communicate in person and via mobilecom, e-mail or any other electronic means available to me in a professional manner with all associates, customers and all those I come in contact with in the course of my employment.

Prohibited Activities. As a driver, I will NOT:

refuse a dispatch for any reason other than hours of service or safety limitations

violate the Federal Motor Carrier Safety Regulations

fuel at locations not on the Company’s designated Fuel Network without the express authorization of my Fleet Manager or the Director of Fuel Programs

make any unauthorized modification to the interior or exterior of the Company tractor to which I am assigned which modification may include but is not limited to placing any placards, lettering, mirrors, lights, etc. on my Company tractor

use my Company tractor or equipment (which includes plates, permits, toll road transponders, mobilecom systems, and other related equipment) for personal, unauthorized or non-dispatched purposes

change or allow change to the factory installed speed governor

use unauthorized or unapproved toll roads, bridges or highways where the cost is charged to the Company without its consent.

e Jam in violation of Company policy and am subject to disciplinary action up to and including termination

POLICY REGARDING MISUSE OF ALCOHOL AND USE OF CONTROLLED SUBSTANCES

In accordance with 49 CFR Part 382.601, the following are the policies and procedures of Crete Carrier Corporation (“Company”) with respect to meeting and exceeding the minimum requirements and regulations of the United States Department of Transportation - Federal Motor Carrier Safety Administration (“DOT” or “FMCSA”) with respect to alcohol and controlled substances, including but not limited to, the regulations relating to Controlled Substances and Alcohol Use and Testing (49 CFR Part 382) and Drug and Alcohol Prohibition (49 CFR Parts 392.4 and 392.5) (“Policy”). Unless otherwise provided herein, the definitions contained in the FMCSA/DOT rules and regulations respecting alcohol and controlled substances shall apply to this Policy.

lL. Contact Person Questions regarding this Policy or about the implementation of this Policy may be directed to the Vice President — Safety & DOT Compliance.

Il. Drivers Subject to Policy This Policy applies to all Company drivers, owner-operators and contractor drivers who operate motor vehicles owned by or leased to the Company and, for purposes of pre-employment/pre-qualification testing, to persons applying for employment as a Company driver or for qualification as an owner- operator or contractor driver.

Il. Prohibited Conduct under FMCSA Rules and Regulations

a.

Pursuant to 49 CFR Part 382.201, no driver shall report for duty or remain on duty requiring the performance of safety-sensitive functions while having an alcohol concentration of 0.04 or greater. Pursuant to 49 CFR Part 382.205, no driver shall use alcohol while performing safety-sensitive functions.

Pursuant to 49 CFR Part 382.207, no driver shall perform safety-sensitive functions within four hours after using alcohol.

Pursuant to 49 CFR Part 382.209, no driver required to take a post-accident alcohol test shall use alcohol for eight hours following the accident, or until he/she undergoes a post-accident alcohol test, whichever occurs first.

Pursuant to 49 CFR Part 382.211, no driver shall refuse to submit to a pre-employment controlled substance test, a post-accident alcohol or controlled substance test, a random alcohol or controlled substance test, a reasonable suspicion alcohol or controlled substance test, a return-to-duty alcohol or controlled substance test, or a follow-up alcohol or controlled substance test.

Pursuant to 49 CFR Part 382.213, no driver shall report for duty or remain on duty requiring the performance of safety-sensitive functions when the driver uses any Schedule | drug or substance or any other non-Schedule | drug or substance, except when the use of any non-Scheduled | controlled substance is pursuant to the instructions of a licensed medical practitioner who is familiar with the driver’s medical history and has advised the driver that the substance will not affect the driver’s ability to safely operate a commercial motor vehicle. It is Company policy that any driver using a therapeutic drug is required to inform the Company of any such use.

Pursuant to 49 CFR Part 382.215, no driver shall report for duty, remain on duty or perform a safety- sensitive function, if the driver tests positive or has adulterated or substituted a test specimen for controlled substances.

Page 1 of 8

Policy Regarding Misuse of Alcohol and Use of Controlled Substances

2/5/2021




IV.

Pursuant to 49 CFR 382.303, no driver involved in an accident in which: (1) there is a fatality; (2) there is bodily injury requiring immediate medical treatment away from the scene and for which the driver receives a citation for a moving traffic violation; or (3) there is disabling damage to a motor vehicle requiring tow away and the driver receives a citation for a moving traffic violation, Shall fail or refuse to be made available for a post-accident alcohol test to be performed within eight hours following the accident or a controlled substance test to be performed within 32 hours following the accident. A driver who is physically able to but who fails or refuses to conduct such test may be deemed by the Company to have refused to submit to testing.

Pursuant to 49 CFR Part 392.4, no driver shall be on duty and possess, be under the influence of, or use, any of the following drugs or other substances: (1) any Schedule | controlled substance, (2) any amphetamine or any formulation thereof, (3) a narcotic drug or any derivative thereof, or (4) any other substance, to a degree which renders the driver incapable of safely operating a motor vehicle. Items (2)-(4) do not apply to the possession or use of a substance administered to a driver by or under the instruction of a licensed medical practitioner who has advised the driver that the substance will not affect the driver’s ability to safely operate a motor vehicle. Possession does not include possession of a substance which is manifested and transported as part of a shipment. Pursuant to 49 CFR Part 392.5(a), no driver shall: (1) use alcohol or be under the influence of alcohol within four hours before going on duty or operating, or having physical control of, a commercial motor vehicle; (2) use alcohol, be under the influence of alcohol, or have any measured alcohol concentration or detected presence of alcohol, while on duty, or operating, or in physical control of a commercial motor vehicle; or (3) be on duty or operate a commercial motor vehicle while the driver possesses alcohol. Possession does not include possession of alcohol which is manifested and transported as part of a shipment.

Safety-Sensitive Function

a.

In accordance with 49 CFR Part 382.107, a “safety-sensitive function” means all time from the time a driver begins to work or is required to be in readiness to work until the time he/she is relieved from work and all responsibility for performing work. Safety-sensitive functions shall include, but are not necessarily limited to:

i. Alltime at a Company or shipper plant, terminal, facility, or other property, or on any public property, waiting to be dispatched, unless the driver has been relieved from duty by the Company;

ii. All time spent conducting pre-trip inspections and post-trip inspections of equipment or otherwise inspecting, servicing, or conditioning any commercial motor vehicle at any time;

iii. All time spent at the driving controls of a commercial motor vehicle in operation;

iv. All time, other than driving time, in or upon any commercial motor vehicle except time resting in a sleeper berth;

v. All time loading or unloading a vehicle, supervising, or assisting in the loading or unloading, attending a vehicle being loaded or unloaded, remaining in readiness to operate the vehicle or in giving or receiving receipts or shipments loaded or unloaded; and

vi. Alltime repairing, obtaining assistance, or remaining in attendance upon a disabled vehicle.

Page 2 of 8

Policy Regarding Misuse of Alcohol and Use of Controlled Substances

2/5/2021




Vi.

Prohibited Conduct under Company Policy

a.

No driver shall operate a Company Vehicle, perform any safety-sensitive functions, or perform any other activity considered to be “on-duty” under FMCSA Hours of Service rules and regulations (49 CFR Part 395.2 (1)-(8)) while the driver is or may be impaired due to the use of alcohol or controlled substance.

No driver shall be in possession of alcohol in any form and at any time while in or on a Company commercial motor vehicle, whether on duty or off duty. A driver shall be deemed to be in possession of alcohol if, at any time, alcohol is located in any part of a Company commercial motor vehicle, including the sleeper berth, but shall not include alcohol being transported as part of a shipment.

No driver shall be in possession of a Schedule | controlled substance or any other controlled substance at any time while in or on a Company Vehicle or on Company premises, whether on duty or off duty, unless such non-Schedule | controlled substance is pursuant to a prescription written to the driver.

No driver shall be under the influence of alcohol or a controlled substance while on Company premises, while using Company property (including a Company Vehicle), or while conducting Company business away from Company premises.

For purposes of this items a-d above, a Company Vehicle shall mean a motor vehicle, including but not limited to a commercial motor vehicle, owned by or leased to the Company.

No driver shall possess, distribute, sell, use, or manufacture illegal drugs or substances.

No driver shall fail to comply with FMCSA/DOT alcohol and controlled substance rules and regulations.

No driver shall refuse to submit to FMCSA or Company alcohol and controlled substance testing. No driver involved in an accident in which: (1) there is a fatality; (2) there is bodily injury requiring immediate medical treatment away from the scene and for which the driver receives a citation for a moving traffic violation; or (3) there is disabling damage to a motor vehicle requiring tow away and the driver receives a citation for a moving traffic violation, shall fail or refuse to report the accident to the Company in a time to permit arrangements to be made for a post-accident alcohol test to be performed within eight hours following the accident or a controlled substance test to be performed within 32 hours following the accident. A driver who is physically able to do so and who fails or refuses to report such an accident to the Company in time to permit arrangements to be made for required post-accident alcohol or controlled substance tests may be considered to have refused to submit to testing.

FMCSA Required Alcohol and Controlled Substance Testing

a.

The Company will conduct a FMCSA required test for the presence of alcohol and/or controlled substances under the following circumstances:

i. Pre-employment testing, pursuant to 49 CFR Part 382.301 — All applicants for employment as a Company driver or for qualification as an owner-operator or contractor driver will be required to submit to controlled substance testing prior to the first time the driver performs safety-sensitive functions for the Company.

ii. Post-accident testing, pursuant to 49 CFR Part 382.303 — Any driver involved in an accident in which: (1) there is a fatality; (2) there is bodily injury requiring immediate medical treatment away from the scene and for which the driver receives a citation for a moving traffic violation; or (3) there is disabling damage to any motor vehicle requiring tow away and the driver receives a citation for a moving traffic violation, will be tested for alcohol and controlled substances as soon as practicable following the accident.

Page 3 of 8

Policy Regarding Misuse of Alcohol and Use of Controlled Substances

2/5/2021




Vil.

Random testing, pursuant to 49 CFR Part 382.305 — The Company will conduct random alcohol and controlled substance tests of at least the percentage of its average number of drivers each year as required by the FMCSA. Drivers will be selected for random testing by a scientifically valid method, which ensures that each driver will have an equal chance of being tested each time selections are made. Consequently, it is possible that an individual driver may be selected more than once each year for random testing. Random alcohol and controlled substance tests will be unannounced and will be conducted on dates spread reasonably throughout the calendar year. Drivers who are selected from random alcohol and/or controlled substances testing are required to proceed immediately to the specified test site.

Reasonable suspicion testing, pursuant to 49 CFR Part 382.307 — A driver will be required to submit to an alcohol or controlled substance test when the Company has a reasonable suspicion that the driver may be under the influence of alcohol or a controlled substance in violation of FMCSA alcohol and controlled substances regulations. The term “reasonable suspicion” includes specific, contemporaneous, articulable observations concerning the driver’s appearance behavior, speech, or body odors by a supervisor or Company official who has received training on the physical, behavioral, speech and performance indicators of probably alcohol misuse and use of controlled substances.

Company Alcohol and Controlled Substance Testing

a. In addition to FMCSA required alcohol and controlled substance testing, the Company may conduct the following testing for the presence of alcohol or controlled substances under the following circumstances:

Pre-employment Hair Follicle Testing — All applicants for employment as a Company driver or for qualification as an owner-operator or contractor driver will be required to undergo controlled substance testing utilizing hair follicle collection.

Reasonable suspicion testing - A driver will be required to undergo an alcohol or controlled substance test when the Company has a reasonable suspicion that the driver may be under the influence of alcohol or a controlled substance in violation of Company policy. The term “reasonable suspicion” includes a reasonable belief that a driver may be using alcohol or controlled substances in violation of Company policy. Among other things, such reasonable belief may be based upon, but is not limited to:

1. Observable phenomena while at work, such as observation of substance abuse or of the physical symptoms or manifestations of being impaired due to substance abuse;

2. Abnormal conduct or erratic behavior while at work or a significant deterioration in work performance;

3. Areport of substance abuse provided by a source the Company reasonably deems to be reliable and credible;

4. Evidence that a driver has tampered with any alcohol or controlled substance test during the driver’s employment;

5. A driver does not report to work on random testing days for no reasonable legitimate reason;

6. Information that a driver has caused or contributed to an accident while at work;

7. Evidence that a driver has used, possessed, sold, solicited or transferred controlled substances while on Company premises, while using Company property or equipment, or while conducting Company business; or

8. Evidence of misuse of alcohol or any legal controlled substances while on Company premises, while using Company property or equipment, or while conducting Company business.

Page 4 of 8

Policy Regarding Misuse of Alcohol and Use of Controlled Substances

2/5/2021




Vill.

Testing Procedures

Testing will be performed in accordance with DOT/FMCSA regulations governing alcohol and controlled

substance testing (49 CFR Parts 40 and 382) including the provisions relating to the integrity of the

testing process, safeguarding the validity of tests results and confidentiality, as applicable.

a. FMCSA Required Alcohol Testing — Alcohol testing will be performed with an evidential breath testing device approved by the National Highway Traffic Safety Administration.

b. FMCSA Required Controlled Substance Testing — FMCSA required controlled substance testing will be performed through urinalysis for the presences of marijuana, cocaine, amphetamines, phencyclidine, and opioids (including the extended opioids oxycodone, oxymorphone, hydrocodone, and hydromorphone) using the split-sample method.

c. Company Alcohol Testing - Alcohol testing will be performed with an evidential breath testing device approved by the National Highway Traffic Safety Administration.

d. Company Controlled Substance Testing:

i. Hair Follicle Testing — Hair follicle testing for the presence of controlled substances will be conducted for the presence of marijuana, cocaine, amphetamines, phencyclidine, and opioids (including the extended opioids oxycodone, oxymorphone, hydrocodone, and hydromorphone) using an independent laboratory. Hair follicle collections will be conducted on or off-site by trained collection personnel, using a collection kit provided by the utilized laboratory and following the collection protocol developed and provided by the utilized laboratory. Hair follicle testing will be conducted using a laboratory accredited to ISO 17025 standards, which evaluate the entire testing process, including confirmatory testing utilizing a mass spectrometry process (GC/MS, GC/MS/MS, and LC/MS/MS). The utilized laboratory will utilize cutoff levels similar to those recommended by the Federal government. The utilized laboratory will report all test results to the Company’s Medical Review Officer by confidential, secure electronic means. The Medical Review Officer will discuss any non-negative result with the driver in a confidential setting. During this discussion, the driver may explain any non-negative result, but the Company reserves the right to strictly enforce this Policy. A driver may request a copy of written test results by making a written request to the attention of Safety Department Records Request, 400 NW 56" Street, Lincoln, Nebraska 68528. Test results are generally considered confidential, but will be provided to the applicant or any person authorized or designated in writing by the applicant; Company vendors, officers, directors, managers, and employees whose work duties require access to such information; and any other mediator, court, or governmental agency (including the FMCSA) as authorized by local, state, or federal law.

ii. Urinalysis - Company controlled substance testing utilizing urinalysis will test for the presences of marijuana, cocaine, amphetamines, phencyclidine, and opioids (including the extended opioids oxycodone, oxymorphone, hydrocodone, and hydromorphone) using the split-sample method. Testing will be performed in accordance with applicable law including any provisions relating to the integrity of the testing process, safeguarding the validity of tests results and confidentiality.

Page 5 of 8

Policy Regarding Misuse of Alcohol and Use of Controlled Substances

2/5/2021




IX.

Mandatory Compliance / Refusal

a. Compliance with the alcohol and controlled substance testing requirements set forth in this Policy is mandatory.

b. Pursuant to 49 CFR Part 382.107, the following constitutes refusal to submit to an alcohol or controlled substance test:

vi.

Vii.

viii. ix.

Failure to appear for any test (except a pre-employment test) within a reasonable time, as determined by the Company, after being directed to do so by the Company;

Failure to remain at the testing site until the testing process is complete. Provided, that a driver who leaves the testing site before the testing process commences for a pre- employment test is not deemed to have refused a test;

Failure to provide a urine specimen for any controlled substances test. Provided, that a driver who does not provide a urine specimen because he/she has left the testing site before the testing process commences for a pre-employment test is not deemed to have refused a test;

The failure to permit the observation or monitoring of a driver’s provision of a urine specimen in the case of a directly observed or monitored collection;

Failure to provide a sufficient amount of urine when directed, and it has been determined, through a required medical evaluation, that there was no adequate medical explanation for the failure;

Failure or declination to take a second test the Company or collector has directed the driver to take;

Failure to undergo a medical examination or evaluation, as directed by the Medical Review Officer (MRO) or as directed by the Designated Employer Representative (DER) after failure to provide a sufficient amount of urine. Provided, in the case of a pre-employment controlled substances test, a driver is deemed to have refused to test on this basis only if the pre-employment test is conducted following a contingent offer of employment; Failure to cooperate with any part of the testing process; or

A report by the MRO of a verified adulterated or substituted test result.

c. Pursuant to Company policy, refusal or failure to present or remain for testing, to complete and sign the breath alcohol or controlled substance testing form, to provide a specimen, to provide an adequate amount of specimen, or otherwise to cooperate with any testing process may be determined to constitute a refusal to submit to testing. A driver, subject to post-accident testing, who does not remain readily available for such testing, may be deemed to have refused to submit to testing. With respect to hair follicle testing, any driver who cooperates with the testing process, but is unable to provide an adequate sample of hair, due to a medical condition or otherwise, may not be considered to have refused to submit to testing, but will be subject to Company protocol regarding retesting or alternative testing. Any driver who fails to provide an adequate sample of hair after attempted retesting may be considered to have refused to submit to testing.

Consequences of Non-Compliance a. FMCSA Consequences of Non-Compliance:

Pursuant to 49 CFR Part 382.501, a driver who engages in conduct prohibited by 49 CFR Part 382 shall be removed from performing any safety-sensitive functions, including driving a commercial motor vehicle. Pursuant to 49 CFR Part 382.503, a driver who engages in conduct prohibited by 49 CFR Part 382 may not resume performing any safety-sensitive functions until the driver completes a Substance Abuse Professional (SAP) evaluation, referral, and education/treatment process as set forth in 49 CFR Part 40, Subpart O.

Page 6 of 8

Policy Regarding Misuse of Alcohol and Use of Controlled Substances

2/5/2021




Xl.

XIl.

ii. Pursuant to 49 CFR Part 382.505, a driver who undergoes an alcohol test and who is found to have an alcohol concentration of 0.02 or greater but less than 0.04 shall not be permitted to drive or perform any other safety-sensitivity function for a period of 24 hours following administration of the test.

iii. Pursuant to 49 CFR Part 392.5(c), a driver who engages in conduct prohibited by 49 CFR Part 392.5 shall be placed out-of-service immediately for a period of 24 hours commencing upon issuance of an out-of-service order issued by a State or Federal official. Pursuant to 49 CFR Part 392.5(d), any driver who is issued an out-of-service order shall: (1) report such issuance to the Company within 24 hours and (2) report such issuance to a State official designated by the State which issued the driver’s license within 30 days unless the driver chooses to request review of the order.

b. Company Consequences of Non-Compliance:

i. A driver who engages in any prohibited conduct under this Policy is subject to disciplinary action up to and including disqualification and termination of employment or cancelation of lease agreement.

Effects of Alcohol and Controlled Substance Use & Referral / Evaluation and Treatment

Information concerning the effects of alcohol and controlled substance use on an individual’s health, work and personal life; signs and symptoms of an alcohol or a controlled substance problem; and available methods of intervening when an alcohol or a controlled substance problem is suspected will be made available to each driver through orientation training. Drivers who have engaged in conduct prohibited by FMCSA rules and regulations will be provided with information regarding resources available to the driver for evaluating and resolving problems associated with the misuse of alcohol and controlled substances. The Company is not required to, and will not, provide or pay for rehabilitation or hold a job open for a driver who is terminated/disqualified for violation of this Policy or FMCSA/DOT alcohol and controlled substance rules and regulations.

Reporting to FMCSA Commercial Driver’s License Drug and Alcohol Clearinghouse Effective January 6, 2020, the following personal information will be reported by the Company to the FMCSA Commercial Driver’s License Drug and Alcohol Clearinghouse: a. Averified positive, adulterated, or substituted drug test result; b. An alcohol confirmation test with a concentration of 0.04 or higher; c. Arefusal to submit to any FMCSA required pre-employment, post-accident, random, or reasonable suspicion alcohol or controlled substance test; d. The Company’s report of actual knowledge of: i. On duty alcohol use pursuant to 49 CFR Part §382.205; ii. Pre-duty alcohol use pursuant to 49 CFR Part §382.207; iii. Alcohol use following an accident pursuant to 49 CFR Part §382.209; and iv. Controlled substance use pursuant to 49 CFR §382.213; e. A Substance Abuse Professional (SAP) report of the successful completion of the return-to-duty process; f. Anegative return-to-duty test; and g. The Company’s report of completion of follow-up testing.

ACKNOWLEDGEMENT OF POLICY REGARDING MISUSE OF ALOCHOL AND USE OF CONTROLLED SUBSTANCES

| hereby acknowledge and certify that | have received a copy of the Crete Carrier Corporation Policy Regarding Misuse of Alcohol and Use of Controlled Substances.

| hereby acknowledge that, in accordance with 49 CFR Part 391.23 and 49 CFR Part 40, each as applicable, Crete Carrier Corporation is authorized and required to release to DOT-regulated employer(s) the following DOT-regulated testing items, including pre-employment testing results, occurring during the previous three years: i) alcohol tests with a result of 0.04 or higher; (ii) verified positive drug tests; (iii) refusals to be tested (including adulterated and/or substituted tests); (iv) other violations of FMCSA/DOT drug and alcohol testing regulations (i.e., violations of 49 CFR 382 Subpart B); (v) information obtained from previous employers of a drug and alcohol rule violation; and (vi) any documentation of completion of the return-to-duty process following a rule violation.

In addition, | hereby acknowledge that, in accordance with 49 CFR Part 382.601(12), Crete Carrier Corporation is authorized and required to release the following DOT-regulated testing items, including pre-employment testing results, to the FMCSA Commercial Driver’s License Drug and Alcohol Clearinghouse: (i) A verified positive, adulterated, or substituted drug test result; (ii) an alcohol confirmation test with a concentration of 0.04 or higher; (iii) a refusal to submit to any test required by subpart C of 49 CFR Part 382; (iv) Crete Carrier Corporation’s actual knowledge of on duty alcohol use pursuant to 49 CFR Part 382.205, pre-duty alcohol use pursuant to 49 CFR Part 382.207, alcohol use following an accident pursuant to 49 CFR Part 382.209, and controlled substance use pursuant to 49 CFR Part 382.213; (v) a substance abuse professional (SAP) report of the successful completion of the return-to-duty process; (vi) a negative return-to-duty test; and (vii) an employer’s report of completion of follow-up testing.

| further hereby acknowledge that Crete Carrier Corporation is authorized by 49 CFR Part 382.405(g) to disclose information regarding alcohol tests with a concentration result of 0.04 or greater, positive controlled substance test results and refusals to be tested (including, but not limited to, adulterated and/or substituted test results) to the decision maker in any lawsuit, grievance, or administrative proceeding | may initiate, or which is initiated on my behalf, arising from the results of a positive FMCSA/DOT alcohol and/or controlled substance test or a refusal to test (including, but not limited to, adulterated or substituted test results) including, but not limited to, claims for unemployment compensation, worker’s compensation, or other proceeding relating to benefits sought. Additionally, Crete Carrier Corporation may disclose information in criminal or civil actions in accordance with 49 CFR. §40.323(a)(2).

| further authorize Crete Carrier Corporation to disclose information regarding any non-FMCSA/DOT alcohol or controlled substance tests and refusals to be tested, including hair follicle tests, to the decision maker or any other parties or persons relating to any lawsuit, grievance, or administrative proceeding; criminal or civil actions; or any other legal matters or proceedings, whether or not initiated by me.

Functional Job Description

Job Title Driver

Company Crete Carrier Corporation/Shaffer Trucking

Employer Job Id

Job Objective Safely and efficiently operate diesel powered tractor trailer combination to transport and deliver products or materials in

packaged or bulk form to and from customer location Hours of Work Up to 14 hrs. per day subject to DOT hours of service requirements

Clothing Steel toe/slip resistant footwear with ankle support, hard hat, safety glasses, gloves, long sleeve shirts, safety vest and other safety gear as required according to customer site policy specification

Equipment/Tools Various commercial tractor cabs, dry or refrigerated trailer units, various bulk or packaged products/materials, manual pallet jacks, pallets, load locks, company invoices, tire chains (equipment included in job, but not limited to the listing), wheel chocks, hand tools, flashlight

Essential Job Functions: Function slide tandems and hook/unhook truck from dry van or refrigerated trailer Activity manually crank lever to raise and lower landing gear 3-4 times/shift Forward Bending Standing (Rarely) for 1 min. while operating the lever.

Pushing (Rarely) vertical with a force of 66 Ib. lifting a 25,000 Ib. load in low gear using a crank with vertical rotation in a radius of 21-51 in. Can use a pushing motion, a pulling motion, or both to accomplish this task.

Activity access and manually release fifth wheel 3-4 times/shift Walking (Rarely) outdoors for 20 ft.

Pulling (Rarely) horizontal at a height of 43 in. with a force of 101 Ib. on a trailer loaded with 25,000 Ibs. Can be performed from a bending position using one hand (35 in. forward reach) or from a standing position using a 5th wheel tool and both hands.

Activity access and manually release tandem pins/levers 3-4 times/shift

Forward Bending Standing (Rarely) to access tandem pins. Can also squat, kneel, or half-kneel as preferred using kneepads and upper extremity assistance when changing positions.

Reach (Rarely) up and forward up to 30 in. in order to grasp the tandem pin.

Pulling (Rarely) at heights ranging from 32-38.5 inches and horizontal pulling forces ranging from 45-139 Ibs to release horizontal tandem pins.

Pulling (Rarely) vertical at a height of 20 in. with a force of 124 Ib. to release vertical tandem levers upward from 20- 36 in.

Activity manually connect/disconnect airlines and power cords and manipulate toggle on/off switch for reefer

Elevated Work (Rarely) for 30 sec. at a height up to 84 in. using preferred hand to operate reefer refrigeration controls at 84 in. height.

Hand Grip (Rarely) static grip at a width of 5 in. with a force of 64 lb. performed at 17 in above the catwalk or 31 in above the ground to connect/disconnect airlines and power cords, using the preferred hand.

Function conduct a daily safety inspection of truck and trailer to insure safe operation of all equipment according to DOT regulations

Activity perform walk around, access underneath and visually inspect truck, dry van and refrigerated unit, electrical connections, brakes and fill out DVIR forms

Walking (Rarely) outdoors for 170 ft. Forward Bending Standing (Rarely) outdoors for 90 sec. inspecting brakes, Sth wheel pin, tires, and connections.

Low Work (Rarely) for 1 min. outdoors may crouch, half-kneel, or kneel. May use kneepads. May use upper extremities when changing positions.

Activity open/close truck hood to check fluid levels and refill as needed

Pulling (Rarely) horizontal at a height of 43 in. with a force of 18 Ib. to open a hood release from the side on tractors where the release is horizontal.

Pulling (Rarely) vertical/upward at a height of 43 in. with a force of 37 Ib. to open a hood release from the side on tractors where the release is vertical.

Pulling (Rarely) to open a hood by pulling upward/vertical. Forces required varied from 16-36 lbs. at 39-43 in. heights

Carry (Rarely) 13 lb. carrying the lock 65 feet from the cab to the back of the trailer; may carry in either or both hands. Pushing (Rarely) horizontal at a height of 61 in. with a force of 57 lb. to push the lock closed. Pulling (Rarely) horizontal at a height of 61 in. with a force of 40 lb. to pull the lock open. Carry (Rarely) 11 lb. for a distance of 15.0 ft. carrying the lock from the cab to the front of the trailer. Can carry in either or both hands.

Pushing (Rarely) horizontal at a height of 44 in. with a force of 21 lb. to engage the lock under the front of the trailer. Activity transport and position wheel chocks

Floor To Waist Lift (Rarely) 10 lb. outdoors wheel chocks are in pairs. These are lifted from the ground and carried at a comfortable height according to Driver preference.

Carry (Rarely) 10 Ib. outdoors wheel chocks are in pairs. Distance carried varies according to customer worksite. Can be carried in either or both hands.

Activity latch/unlatch ratchet straps Pushing (Rarely) horizontal with a force of 78 Ib. ratcheting straps tight or loosening them at heights up to 72 in. Pulling (Rarely) horizontal with a force of 78 lb. ratcheting straps tight or loosening them at heights up to 72 in. Activity block and brace freight for transit Hand Grip (Rarely) static grip with a force of 82 Ib. using the preferred hand driving nails using a | lb. claw hammer. Pulling (Rarely) horizontal at a height of 24 in. with a force of 25 Ib. pulling nails using a 3 Ib. /24 in crowbar. Activity latch/unlatch trailer swing doors and secure open with hooks Pushing (Rarely) vertical at a height of 52 in. with a force of 38 Ib. to open the latch.

Pulling (Rarely) horizontal at a height of 65 in. with a force of 6 Ib. to open the swing doors. Bilateral Hand Coordination (Rarely) to secure the swing door with hooks.

Activity manually open/close trailer back roll up door when present Pushing (Rarely) vertical at a height of 60 in. with a force of 45 lb. pushing upward to open the door. Pulling (Rarely) vertical at a height of 72 in. with a force of 40 Ib. pulling downward to close the door. Activity clean trailer and cab Sitting (Rarely) for 1 min. while sitting on a vehicle seat to pick up items inside the cab. Forward Bending Sitting (Rarely) for 1 min. while sitting on a vehicle seat to pick up items from the floor of the cab. Standing (Rarely) for 5 min. to sweep out the trailer.

Pushing/Pulling (Rarely) horizontal at a self-selected height with a force of 4 lb. sweeping the trailer using a broom;

Function transport freight from customer origin to customer destination Activity enter and exit cab using 3 point contact Stair Climbing (Occasionally) 3 steps. Step heights vary from 13.5-19 in. depending on the tractor model.

Activity steer and maneuver gear controls, brake system and clutch to safely drive truck in all conditions according to DOT regulations and maintain required valid CDL Class A license issued in state of residence and without state restrictions.

Sitting (Frequently) while driving for up to 11 hrs. Bilateral Hand Grip (Frequently) dynamic grip with a force of 25 Ib. to operate vehicle hand controls. Bilateral Hand Coordination (Frequently) to operate the vehicle hand controls.

Bilateral Foot Controls (Frequently) depress clutch, brake, and accelerator requiring 12-84 lbs. of force depending on the pedal depressed, the tractor model, and the tractor condition.

Function prepare trailer for unloading from rear of trailer. This includes opening the trailer doors and accessing the trailer as when securing the freight.

Activity position bulkheads on reefer trailers

Pulling (Rarely) vertical at a height of 57 in. with a force of 42 Ib. diagonal pull-down from the trailer ceiling to lower the bulkheads.

Pushing (Rarely) vertical at a height of 49.5 in. with a force of 21 Ib. upward push to release bulkheads from the trailer ceiling.

Pulling (Rarely) horizontal at a height of 45 in. with a force of 39 Ib. to slide bulkheads along their tracks.

Pushing (Rarely) horizontal at a self-selected height with a force of 16 lb. to secure bulkheads in desired position. Activity restack or stair step freight as needed

Floor To Waist Lift (Occasionally) 75 Ib. to 42 in. boxes weighing 50-75 Ibs are stacked to up 50 in height.

Waist To Crown Lift (Occasionally) 50 Ib. to 72 in. freight weighing up to 50 Ibs. may be stacked to 72 in. height. Activity sort and stage freight within the trailer using a manual pallet jack with an 800 Ib. load on a level surface

Pushing (Rarely) with a force of 32 lb. at a downward diagonal angle starting at 48 in. height to raise the pallet off the floor.

Pulling (Rarely) horizontal with a force of 50 Ib. up to pull the pallet up to 30 feet at a self-selected height 48 in. or lower.

Pushing (Rarely) horizontal with a force of 37 Ib. to push the pallet jack up to 30 feet at a self-selected height 48 in. or lower.

Activity sort and stage windows, insulation, and doors for unloading

Pulling (Rarely) horizontal at a height of 72 in. with a force of 26 lb. pulling 77.5 square foot rolls of insulation off a stack up to 72 in high and letting them drop to the floor.

Pushing (Rarely) horizontal at a self-selected height with a force of 36 lb. up sliding doors with glass panels (6 ft x 6 ft 8 in)-36 lbs or 28x54 in windows-18 lbs. across the trailer bed for distances up to 53 feet.

Activity manually shrink wrap pallets Standing (Rarely) Forward Bending Standing (Rarely) Front Carry (Rarely) 15 lb. for a distance of 100.0 ft.

Waist To Crown Lift (Rarely) 15 Ib. to 72 in. applying shrink wrap on loads up to 72 in. high. Activity operate customer manual roll-up bay doors where electric or chain-operated doors are not available

Pulling (Rarely) to raise a roll-up door part way (will be pushed up the remainder). Pull downward on ropes from 14-25 in. height and requires 49-94 Ibs. of vertical force, depending on the type and condition of each door.

Pushing (Rarely) vertical with a force of 59 Ib. pushing the doors upward at heights from 54-56 in, requiring 32-59 lbs. of upward vertical force depending on the type and condition of each door.

Pulling (Rarely) vertical with a force of 59 lb. downward at heights 74-80 in. requiring 35.1-59.2 lbs. of force to close the doors depending on the type and condition of each door.

Pulling (Rarely) vertical with a force of 25 Ib. to secure bungee cords.

JOB TITLE: Driver (Crete/Shaffer) PREPARED DATE: 10/8/14

SUMMARY Safely and efficiently operate diesel powered tractor trailer combination to transport and deliver products or materials in packaged or bulk form. ESSENTIAL DUTIES AND RESPONSIBILITIES include the following. Other duties may be assigned.

e Qualifies as an over the road driver pursuant to U.S. Department of Transportation (“DOT”) regulations and policies. Manages tractor, trailer or freight in his/her possession. Loads or unloads trailers with interstate and intrastate loads of freight at various shippers and receivers. Operates Class 8 tractor trailer combination from origin to destination including driving, sliding tandems, hook/unhook, etc.. Inspects tractor and trailer for defects as needed and required by DOT and submits report indicating truck condition pursuant to DOT regulations and company policies. Maintains and provides the company a daily record of duty status pursuant to DOT regulations and company policies. Present tractor and trailers (as applicable) for scheduled and unscheduled maintenance. Assists workers in loading and unloading tractor trailer as required. Complies with the requirements in the Driver’s Handbook and General Rules of Conduct. Periodically shags trailers to and from customer locations for loading or unloading and performs other duties as assigned. Receives and carries out instructions. Maintains regular and predictable attendance.

salir sae: SKILLS AND ABILITIES Ability to read, write and speak English and hear in accordance with DOT regulations. e Ability to see in accordance to the DOT’s regulations. e = Ability to sit, walk, balance, twist, bend, climb, lift, carry, push/pull, grip, kneel, crouch and crawl, all as set forth in the Driver Functional Job Description. e = Ability to add, subtract, multiply and divide. e General knowledge and proficient use of a computer and computer programs.

EDUCATION AND/OR EXPERIENCE

High school diploma or general education degree (GED) preferred; and acceptable over the road tractor trailer experience or proof of graduation from a Qualified School Training Program and successful completion of over the road driving with a certified company driver trainer pursuant to the student program.

CERTIFICATES, LICENSES, REGISTRATIONS

Commercial Driver’s License

Hazardous Material Endorsement required for certain fleets

Current DOT Medical Examination Report and Physical Medical Card

Qualified Truck Driving Program Certificate for Students without previous CDL driving experience

WORK ENVIRONMENT The nature of the environment is one in which the employee may come in contact with outside weather conditions, vibration, moving mechanical parts, fumes or airborne particles, toxic or caustic chemicals, extreme cold or extreme heat and excessive noise levels.

Certification of Compliance with Driver License Requirements

Motor Carrier Instructions: The requirements in Part 383 apply to every driver who operates in intrastate, interstate, or foreign commerce and operates a vehicle weighing or rated at 26,001 pounds or more, can transport more than 15 people, or transports hazardous materials that require placarding.

The requirements in Part 391 apply to every driver who operates in interstate commerce and operates a vehicle weighing or rated at 10,001 pounds or more, can transport more than 15 people (or more than 8 people when there is direct compensation), or transports hazardous materials that require placarding.

Driver Requirements: Parts 383 and 391 of the Federal Motor Carrier Safety Regulations contain certain driver licensing requirements that you as a driver must comply with, including the following:

1. Possess only one license: You, as a commercial vehicle driver, may not possess more than one motor vehicle operator’s license.

2. Notification of License suspension, revocation or cancellation: Sections 391.15 (b)(2) and 383.33 of the Federal Motor Carrier Safety Regulations require that you notify your employer the NEXT BUSINESS DAY of any revocation, suspension, cancellation or disqualification of your driver’s license or driving privilege. In addition, Section 383.31 requires that any time you are convicted of violating a state or local traffic law (other than parking), you must report it within 30 days to your employing motor carrier. The notification must be made in writing.

3. CDL Domicile Requirement: Section 383.23 (a)(2) requires that your commercial driver’s license be issued by your legal state of domicile, where you have your true, fixed, and permanent home and principal residence and to which you have the intention of returning whenever you are absent. If you establish a new domicile in another state, you must apply to transfer your CDL within 30 days.

DEPARTMENT OF TRANSPORTATION PHYSICAL POLICY

Company policy at Crete Carrier Corporation and its operating division Shaffer Trucking (“the Company”) requires that all Department of Transportation re-certification physicals be completed by a Company approved DOT physician at one of the Company’s terminal locations. The Company pays for Company driver re-certification physicals. Owner operator/lease driver re-certification physicals will be charged back to the owner of the tractor.

Drivers who have a Body Mass Index (BMI) of 35 kg/m2 or greater based on information as determined from the DOT physical completed by a Company approved DOT physician will be required to complete a sleep study, unless already diagnosed with Obstructive Sleep Apnea (OSA). Drivers diagnosed with OSA as a result of such sleep study and who are prescribed a PAP treatment device will be required to regularly transmit usage data and comply with the treatment standards.

Drivers diagnosed with a OSA and using a PAP treatment device are often required by DOT physicians to submit a usage history showing sufficient usage of the PAP device prior to being qualified by the DOT physician. Therefore, prior to a recertification physical, any driver utilizing a PAP device will be required to have obtained a usage history for the DOT physician's review during the recertification physical. Usage history varies by DOT physician. Therefore, a driver should be prepared to supply a minimum history of 30 days, and in some cases, may be required to supply 90 or more days of history.

Drivers who are physically qualified to operate a commercial motor vehicle with a diagnosis of diabetes mellitus treated with insulin for control under 49 CFR 391.41 (b)(3) under must self-monitor blood glucose levels in accordance with the specific treatment plan prescribed by the driver’s treating clinician. Such levels must be measured with an electronic glucometer that stores all readings, that records the date and time of readings, and from which data can be electronically downloaded. Any driver with a diagnosis of diabetes mellitus treated with insulin for control must, as soon as reasonably practicable, report to the Company and the driver’s treating clinician any occurrence of a severe hypoglycemic episode. A severe hypoglycemic episode is one that requires the assistant of others, or results in loss of consciousness, seizure, or coma.

DRIVER’S RECEIPT AND ACKNOWLEDGEMENT I hereby certify that I have received a copy of the Company’s Policy Regarding Department of Transportation Physicals.

Disclosure and Authorization for Procurement/Release of Information for Employment Purposes — 49 CFR Part 391.23 DOT Drug/Alcohol

Testing: In accordance with DOT Regulation 49 CFR Part 391.23 and 49 CFR Part 40, each as applicable, | hereby authorize release of my DOT-regulated drug and alcohol testing records by my past or present DOT-regulated employer(s) to Crete Carrier Corporation. | understand that information/documents released pursuant to this section is limited to the following DOT-regulated testing items, including pre-employment testing results, occurring during the previous three (3) years: (i) alcohol tests with a result of 0.04 or higher; (ii) verified positive drug tests; (iii) refusals to be tested (including adulterated and/or substituted tests); (iv) other violations of DOT drug and alcohol testing regulations (i.e., violations of 49 CFR 382 Subpart B); (v) information obtained from previous employers of a drug and alcohol rule violation; and (vi) any documentation of completion of the return-to-duty process following a rule violation. Consent for Limited Queries of the Federal Motor Carrier Safety Administration (FMCSA) Drug and Alcohol Clearinghouse

I hereby provide consent to Crete Carrier Corporation and its division of Shaffer Trucking (hereinafter collectively referred to as "Crete Carrier Corporation") to conduct a limited query of the FMCSA Commercial Driver's License Drug and Alcohol Clearinghouse to determine whether drug or alcohol violation information about me exists in the Clearinghouse. I understand this consent shall remain on file and shall serve as ongoing consent for Crete Carrier Corporation to conduct multiple limited queries of the Clearinghouse at any time during my employment or contract period without asking me for additional consent.

I understand that if I refuse to provide consent for Crete Carrier Corporation to conduct a limited query of the Clearinghouse, Crete Carrier Corporation is required to prohibit me from performing safety-sensitive functions, including operating a commercial motor vehicle.

I understand that if the limited query conducted by Crete Carrier Corporation indicates that drug or alcohol information exists about me in the Clearinghouse, the FMCSA will not disclose that information to Crete Carrier Corporation unless I give additional specific consent within the Clearinghouse. However, I understand that Crete Carrier Corporation will be required to conduct a full query of the Clearinghouse within 24 hours after a limited query indicates that drug or alcohol information exists and that if I do not grant consent within the Clearinghouse for that full query I will be removed from performing safety-sensitive functions, including operating a commercial motor vehicle.

Consent for Limited Queries of the Federal Motor Carrier Safety Administration (FMCSA) Drug and Alcohol Clearinghouse

I hereby provide consent to Crete Carrier Corporation and its division of Shaffer Trucking (hereinafter collectively referred to as "Crete Carrier Corporation") to conduct a limited query of the FMCSA Commercial Driver's License Drug and Alcohol Clearinghouse to determine whether drug or alcohol violation information about me exists in the Clearinghouse. I understand this consent shall remain on file and shall serve as ongoing consent for Crete Carrier Corporation to conduct multiple limited queries of the Clearinghouse at any time during my employment or contract period without asking me for additional consent.

I understand that if I refuse to provide consent for Crete Carrier Corporation to conduct a limited query of the Clearinghouse, Crete Carrier Corporation is required to prohibit me from performing safety-sensitive functions, including operating a commercial motor vehicle.

I understand that if the limited query conducted by Crete Carrier Corporation indicates that drug or alcohol information exists about me in the Clearinghouse, the FMCSA will not disclose that information to Crete Carrier Corporation unless I give additional specific consent within the Clearinghouse. However, I understand that Crete Carrier Corporation will be required to conduct a full query of the Clearinghouse within 24 hours after a limited query indicates that drug or alcohol information exists and that if I do not grant consent within the Clearinghouse for that full query I will be removed from performing safety-sensitive functions, including operating a commercial motor vehicle.

Staring Pay; $0.59 per practical mile. Paid ona per-trip basis as compensation for all on-duty activities required to safely and legally deliver a load (including without limitation fueling, inspections, scaling loads, driving, and loading/unloading time less than 2 hours each).

Maximum Base

Mileage Pay: $0.66 per practical mile.

Pay Increases: One Cent ($.01) per practical mile per year if

a) The driver drove at least 108,000 (9,000/month) practical route paid miles in the year ending with the driver’s anniversary date of qualification, and

b) The driver has no more than 12 safety points against the driver’s safety record on the driver’s anniversary date of qualification.

c) Raise computed and effective on anniversary date of qualification.

Short Haul Pay: Eligible Quarterly Bonus: Eligible. 30,000 miles at $0.04/mile. Drop & Stop Pay: Paid at the rate of $30 per stop. Initial pickup and final destination on load are excluded

as stop or drop. Fee is split between team drivers. Detention Pay; Detention is applicable as per the Detention Pay Scale.

Time Out on Road; Generally can expect to be out on the road five (5) to eight (8) days at a time, with your Remaining Days Out (RDO) set at six (6) days. May require weekend pick up or delivery so there is no guarantee of home time during any specific or regular day of the week or weekend. Generally, can plan average home time of approximately 34 to 48 hours. Periodically, will be on home time under a load in order to maximize driver and Company productivity. Special requests for additional time off (vacation, doctor appointments, etc.) must be made through your Asset Manager a minimum five (5) to seven (7) days in advance of needed time off.
